to perform terrain and vegetation mapping. The study 
site is a part of the challenging Mt. Houshanyue 
hiking trail that collapsed after the Sinlaku typhoon 
(September 2008). It is north to a tea plantation and 
near a Taipower 345 kV transmission tower. The total 
area affected by the landslides is about 10 hectares. 
Since slopes evolve continuously as a result of 
natural processes such as wind and water erosion, 
better and faster tools related to generating more 
realistic 3-D representation of the landslide sites 
are desired. Also, since landslides tend to occur at 
the same locations repeatedly (landslide succession), 
terrestrial laser scanning is useful to provide 
constant monitoring of the sites. As the landform 
evolves over time, scans took at different times 
(before and after typhoons and torrential rains) can 
be compared to assess possible landslides and their 
dimensions. Laser scanning can also be used to 
monitor the plant recovery on landslides and to study 
the best method to stabilize the slopes biologically. 
This will in turn aid the investigation and timely 
assessment of landslide potentials. In contrast to 
traditional surveying techniques, the terrestrial 
laser scanning takes far less time to obtain the 3-D 
information of the target while achieving high 
measurement accuracy at the same time. The data 
collected can be easily processed to create a 3-D 
virtual environment and easily archived for long-term 
monitoring and comparison. The results could be used 
in the subsequent stability analysis of the slope and 
in the long-term monitoring of the landform 
evolution. This research work is a three-year 
project, and this progress report is produced after 
year two. 
英文關鍵詞： terrestrial laser scanner, slopes, typhoons

ᜢᗖຒǺΟᆢႜ৔௟ඔሺǴ஝༥ӦǴཱུᆄ਻ং
Abstract
This research project is in response to the devastating floods/landslides in southern Taiwan due to Typhoon 
Morakot and the call for proposal from the National Science Council. The original proposal passed the first 
round of review, and the detailed proposal was also submitted and passed. At first, four sub-projects were 
proposed. After examining the interrelationship and dependencies between these sub-projects, however, it was 
decided to combine several sub-projects together and invite three more researchers to join the research team. 
As a result the final research project has a total of five sub-projects in addition to the main project, and the 
research team consists of professors from the National Taipei University of Technology (Department of Civil 
Engineering and Department of Computer Science and Information Engineering) and the National Central 
University (Center for Space and Remote Sensing Research). The leaders of these sub-projects will 
collaborate with one another and with the PI of the main project. The aim of this research project was to study 
the landslide site near the MRT Zhinan Temple Station and to perform terrain and vegetation mapping. The 
study site is a part of the challenging Mt. Houshanyue hiking trail that collapsed after the Sinlaku typhoon 
(September 2008). It is north to a tea plantation and near a Taipower 345 kV transmission tower. The total

ҁୢڔଞჹ 4 ᅿόӕӦᗺ܌ܡឪϐቹႽϩձ೛ी፾ӝᚒҞǴаᔠෳڙ၂ޣᢀჸ౜ӦޑૈΚᆶ҅ዴ
܄ǴаΠࣁӚ၂ᚒϐᚒҞȐӅ 9ᚒȑǴ9ঁୢᚒϷ 4ಔቹႽޑϩଛ߄ӵ߄ 3܌ҢǺ
1. Identify gullies. Pick out the gully in the given images and rank the images (one being the highest) 
according to which type gives you a better view of the feature, makes it appear more apparent and 
eases its identification. 
2. Pick out the roots in the given images and rank the images according to which type gives you a 
better view of the feature, makes it appear more apparent and eases its identification. Can you tell 
the directions of the roots? With what image type are you capable of doing this? 
3. Rock cracks and joints. Take a look at the images provided. Identify the rock joints and cracks. 
Which image type do you prefer to use for such a task? This obviously has to be the image that 
gives you the best possible view of the attributes of the crack or joint such as its nature, depth and 
size. Rate the images in order of preference one being the most preferred. 
4. Tilting of trees. The direction at which the trees tilt can tell us the direction the soil or slope it is 
anchored in is moving towards. With what image type can you precisely tell the direction the trees 
tilts towards? For each image type please write the direction you think the tree tilts towards. Feel 
free to comment on how each image performs in giving you a sense of direction of the objects 
contained within. 
5. Depth and Relative depth. Images can give you a sense of depth of the objects they contain. For 
example you can tell which object between two is closer to or farther from you. You should also be 
able to tell or estimate the relative depths of objects. Which image would be the best tool to use for 
depth calculations? Please give your reasons. 
6. Erosion is the washing away of the top soil normally as a result of wind force or runoff from water. 
Signs of erosion are usually apparent to the naked eye. Can you tell which area is undergoing or has 
undergone erosion from the given image? What images makes the process more visible? Rank the 
images in order of visibility. One being the most visible. 
7. Spatial Localization. With spatial localization you can concentrate on a certain object placed at a 
particular depth while being partially oblivious of other objects in the picture. This helps when you 
want to analyze the object without having your judgment clouded by the presence of other objects. 
Which image among the three brings out the best effects of spatial localization? 
8. Surface curvature. Which Image type displays the curvature of soil surfaces better? 
9. Image quality. The quality of the image plays a very important role in the analysis of objects in the 
image. The higher the quality and resolution, the better the details contained within. Which image is 
of higher quality? Does the image quality play any significant role? Rate the images from 1-3, 1 
being the highest.

IX 
XI 
ABSTRACT
The research is focus on most popularly 3D-Data acquisition technology, such as 
Terrestrial LIDAR, Airborne LIDAR, UAV, Aerial Photogrammetry and Ground 
Photogrammetry. The study area is Hou-shan-yue in Taipei, which provide large-scale 
and small-scale disasters to research, such as collapse of slope and growth track of 
trees. Therefore, every 3D-data acquisition technology can be studied and discussed. 
Multi-source 3D-Data model will be integrated and compared in this research, and 
provided to another sub-project. 
The 3D-Data from different time can be analyzed for slope-change. But 3D-Data 
from different acquisition technology are different sources, resolution, and period. 
Therefore, storage and analysis of 3D-Data are complex. In order to compare and 
analyze multi-source, multi-resolution and multi-period 3D-Data model, capability 
and limit of 3D-Data acquisition technology should be studied 
KeywordǺ3D model, LIDAR, Photogrammetry, slope-change analysis

1ᶨˣ㐀天
忳䓐暟⮬㌫㍷₨ LIDAR (Light Detection and Ranging)ᶵỮ傥㌫㍷⣏䇯⋨➇ˣ䓐㕤䲨抬悥ⶪ⺢䭱䈑
䘬⡆㷃ˣ᷎⎗ẍ㷃⮹慷㷔ⶍ㗪ˤ㛔妰䔓⇑䓐暟⮬㌫㍷₨ LIDAR ㇨慷㷔⇘檀䱦䡢⛘尴屯㕁䘬⍾㧋
溆⺢㥳ㆸᶱ䵕䘬堐朊㧉✳ˤ⮵㕤⛘尴䘬屯㕁炻暨天⮯℠啷䘬⋨➇炻德忶 LIDAR ㌫㍷₨⮯⮎⛘䘬
⟜㘗屯妲姀抬崟Ἦ炻忁ṃ屯妲ᶵ⁭⎗ẍ⺢ㆸ㧉✳ˣ怬傥⺞Ỡㅱ䓐⛐㹹≽↮㜸炻⚈㠭暐ㆾ桙桐㇨忈
ㆸ䘬⛇䞛㳩㹹≽冯ⳑ⟴ˤ⇑䓐 LIDAR ㌫㍷₨炻⎗ẍ↮㗪㭝䘬䲨抬⮎⛘䘬⟜㘗炻⮯忁ṃ⛘⋨㇨㌫
㍷⇘䘬屯妲Ἦ㍊⊀怲✉䘬嬲⊾炻慵⺢䎦⛘䘬⛘尴炻⺢伖⼴䘬屯㕁ℵṌ䓙↮㜸Ṣ⒉忚埴↮㜸ˤ
The LIght Detection And Ranging (LIDAR) can scan large area in a short time with high resolution. 
Heavy urban development changes the landscape dramatically, landscape scanning can record the 
evolution process of urban area and the corresponding increase of buildings and structures. This research 
developed visualization techniques to study topographic changes of hillside, cliff, and riverbed utilizing 
a terrestrial LIDAR system in combination with interactive visualization techniques to present these 
findings. The LIDAR point cloud can be used in slide analysis caused by rain fall or typhoon. It allows 
us to perform monitoring and movement potential accessment.

㭷䫮溆暚悥㚱ᶱᾳ㕳廱奺⹎ᷳ㕡⎹(XˣYˣZ)ẍ⍲ᶱᾳỵ䦣㕡⎹(XˣYˣZ)ℙℕᾳ冒䓙⹎炻忳䓐

䘬溆普嶅暊嬲⼿崲⮷炻忼⇘㓞㔪⼴炻ᶱ䵕䘬溆暚屯㕁⣿䔲⬴ㆸ炻᷎㚫⏰䎦⤥䘬⣿䔲䱦⹎炻Ữ㗗忁
3⁛䴙 ICP 㘖念怑䓐㕤溆暚⮵滲炻Ữ㓞㔪䘬忇⹎⣒ㄊ炻᷎ᶼ⛐➟埴⣿䔲㛇攻炻暨天㏄⮳䚠斄䫎⎰

侴[2]㇨㍸↢㚨⮷⸛㕡惵⮵䘬㕡㱽埵䓇↢㚨⮷⸛㕡⼙⁷䘬惵⮵㕡㱽ˣ䳸⎰ Chetverikov ㇨㍸↢䘬䭙

䣢ἧ䓐䭙⫸䨢攻↯√䘬屯㕁䳸㥳炻妰䬿ᶲḇ⡆≈Ḯℑ军ᶱ᾵ˤ
⮵㕤⁛䴙 ICP ⺢䩳䚠䫎䘬溆普㇨㍉⍾䘬㕡⺷⼨⼨㗗䓐溆冯溆ㆾ溆冯堐朊䘬惵⮵㕡⺷炻惵⮵䘬溆
普㚫⼰⣂炻⮶农㇨剙䘬㗪攻冯㓞㔪忇⹎㚫嬲⼿⼰ㄊ炻⚈㬌[3]ᶵ㍉⍾ ICP ⺢䩳䚠䫎溆普䘬㕡⺷炻
侴㗗ἧ䓐㚱㬋屈㔠䘬嶅暊↥⺷(distance function)㺼䬿㱽Ἦ㯪↢婌ⶖῤ炻㚫ἧ⼿溆普㔠ᶳ旵炻᷎德
忶 Levenberg 㺼䬿㱽⾓忇䘬㷃⮹徕ẋ㫉㔠炻⽆⮎槿≈ℍ悐↮㭼ἳ䘬暄妲⇘㚱慵䔲悐↮䘬溆暚屯㕁炻
䓊䓇䘬⣿䔲ὅ䃞ᶵ⍿⼙枧炻␴⁛䴙 ICP㭼庫⛯㕡㟡婌ⶖ MSE (mean square error)ẍ⍲㓞㔪䘬忇⹎
䘤䎦炻拗婌䌯嬲Ỷᶼ㓞㔪忇⹎庫⾓ˤ
⁛䴙 ICP 㺼䬿㱽⮵㕤㚱暄妲䘬溆暚㚫忈ㆸ⣿䔲ᶵἛ䘬䳸㝄炻⮵㕤䚠䫎䘬溆普ḇ㚫㚱慵墯ㆾ嶅暊
⣒怈悥㗗⼙⁷⣿䔲䘬⚈䳈炻᷎ᶼἧ䓐溆暚䘬慵⽫ᷕ溆䔞ἄ⍫侫溆⼰⭡㖻怠㑯⇘暄妲䘬溆普炻䁢Ḯ

Ӆ41। ಃ2।
मЎᄔा
KeywordsǺ Digital Elevation Model, ChiChi earthquake, Typhoon Morakot, Numerical Modeling, 
Ground LIDAR 
Taiwan, due to the frequent typhoons, high seismicity and high annual rainfall, numerous landslides 
triggered every year and severe impacts affect the island. Concerning to the catastrophic landslides, the 
key information of landslide, including range of landslide, volume estimation and the subsequent 
evolution are important when analyzing the triggering mechanism, hazard assessment and mitigation.  
Based on this purpose, the morphological analysis gives a general overview for the landslides and 
been considered as one of the most fundamental information. Based on above reasons, the research is 
aimed at structuring a 2m DTM consisting of the landform before and after landslides, and the rebuilding 
by exploiting aerial image and positioning system with precise LIDAR coordinates loaded to measure 
control point and mobile Remotely Piloted Vehicle image data. Furthermore, according to the Digital 
Terrain Model (DTM), the Precision Control Index is used to evaluate the DSM Average Vertical Error, 
Standard Deviation, Worse Maximum, and Worse Minimum, forming Error Normal Distribution whose 
Peak Graph help us ensure that the accuracy is in ideal condition. The range of evaluation includes the 
whole area, slide land and skirts of the slide land to find the difference among three sections. 
We compare the variations of altitude from 2005 to 2010 by constructing DSM analyzing 
topographic change in every period and using the search function of Arc Map obtaining Surface Elevation 
of longitudinal section and transverse section. Besides, orthoimage is also exploited to detect the range of 
wood erosion. 
KeywordsǺDigtial Terrain Model, Houshanyue, Precision Assessment

1／2 2012/8/25 下午 02:34
Scripting STABL with PSO for Analysis of Slope 
Stability 
Zhe-Ping Shen, Jian-An Wang, Walter Chen
1
 and Fuan Tsai2 
 
1
 Dept. of Civil Engineering/LiDAR Center for High Performance Visualization and 
Disaster Research, National Taipei University of Technology, Taipei, Taiwan  
{fishfishfishgoo@gmail.com, petera23p@yahoo.com.tw, waltchen@ntut.edu.tw} 
 
2
 Center for Space and Remote Sensing Research, National Central University, Zhongli, 
Taiwan  
ftsai@csrsr.ncu.edu.tw  
Abstract. Landslide is a recurring problem in Taiwan as well as other parts of 
the world, which kills many persons every year. The more developed the 
societies, the more vulnerable they are to the occurrences of natural disasters. 
That is why the analysis of slope stability continues to receive high attention 
amongst researchers. In this study, the authors aimed to use the standard 
landslide analysis program (STABL) and turned it into a computation engine 
for PSO. A scripting program and a batch file were written to control the 
execution of STABL. The results of STABL were automatically analyzed by 
the scripting program to produce next generation's input data files. After testing 
the system on a standard soil slope, the result showed very promising potentials. 
Not only did the system converge to a solution, but it also generated the best 
solution ever in the literature.  
Keywords: Slope stability, STABL, PSO, landslides 
1   Introduction 
Landslide is a recurring problem in Taiwan as well as other parts of the world, which 
kills many persons every year [1]. Although natural disasters such as landslides 
usually cause more casualties in less developed countries than in more affluent ones, 
no country is immune to the threat. On the contrary, economically more developed 
countries tend to invest more on sophisticated technologies and infrastructure systems 
such as telecommunication systems, electric power, municipal water, and 
transportation networks, and the smooth working of their societies depend heavily on 
the proper functioning of these systems. Any slight disruption to one of these systems 
can put the country's economy in crisis and trigger a tremendous financial reaction. 
This actually makes modern societies more vulnerable to the occurrences of natural 
disasters. Since landslide is a natural phenomenon that will not cease to exist, more 
insightful analysis will benefit everyone now and in the future.  
 Fig. 1. Conceptual diagram showing the mapping from the physical space of a slope to an 
imaginary 2-D solution space where PSO can be applied to determine the best solution. 
 
Fig. 2. Conceptual diagram showing the use of a scripting program to control the execution of 
STABL, a slope stability analysis program developed by Purdue University. 
Equation (1) was used in the PSO scripting program (written in Fortran) and the 
parameters related to swarms or particles were kept as simple as possible. The main 
reason is that this study is a proof of concept on obtaining the most critical sliding 
surface using the existing de facto analysis program (STABL) instead of writing a 
new analysis program to incorporate PSO directly in the computation of FS. It is 
drastically different from the approach taken by references [1-2]. As can be seen from 
Figure 3, the interactive STABL was forced to run in the batch mode. The names and 
contents of the input files that used to be entered by a user are now prepared by the 
scripting program. The output files from STABL were also fed to the scripting 
program to extract the values of FS. The entire process is looped continuously until 
the convergence criterion is met for FS.  
4   Computational Results  
In order to test the computation framework proposed by this study, a sample soil 
slope was chosen from the literature. This particular slope had been the subject of 
many studies and a good summary was provided by [6]. The slope itself is 5 m high 
with a simple profile (will be shown later in the final results). The authors used 10 
particles in the simulation. In order to encompass as vast an area as possible, the left 
end point was allowed to vary from 0 to 5 m, and the right end point was allowed to 
change in the range between 15 and 25 m. Within these two ranges, the particles were 
spread out. After around 90 iterations, the entire group of particles converged to the 
same minimum FS of 1.238. A typical convergence curve is shown in Figure 4 for 
particle #10, and the trace of its movement is produced in Figure 5. Remember from 
Figure 1, the 2-D space shown in Figure 5 is the mapping result of the physical space 
to the solution space. The X and Y coordinates denote the left end and the right end 
point of the sliding surface, respectively. The particle #10 started near the upper right-
hand corner and eventually converged to the final location near the lower right-hand 
corner. The most critical sliding surface corresponding to the solution of this study is 
plotted in Figure 6 along with the sliding surfaces obtained by other studies in the 
literature. A good match is noticed between various sliding surfaces. In addition, the 
minimum FS obtained in this study is 1.238, which is lower than the 1.325-1.329 
obtained by Cheng et al. [6]. The FS is also lower than the 1.327-1.348 reported in the 
literature and summarized in [6]. The only other study that yielded as low an FS as 
this study is by Malkawi et al. [7]. Their FS is the exact same 1.238. No other 
research has reported a lower FS. 
5   Conclusions and Future Work 
In this study, the authors proposed a method to utilize the existing authoritative slope 
stability analysis program, STABL, to perform PSO simulations. STABL was chosen 
because the results generated by STABL are credible and unlike programs written in-
house no further testing was needed to verify the FS's. The analysis framework was 
based on a scripting program developed by the authors to control the execution of

Run-Time GPU Computing and Rendering of Earthquake Ground-Motion Data
Ming-Da Chen and Tung-Ju Hsieh
Department of Computer Science and Information Engineering
National Taipei University of Technology
Taipei, Taiwan
Email: t8598007@ntut.edu.tw, tjh@csie.ntut.edu.tw
Abstract—Earthquake simulations generate large-scale
ground-motion velocity data. However, in addition to the
ground-motion velocity data, seismologists also need to study
both ground-motion acceleration and ground-motion displace-
ment data. Therefore, data post-processing is required to dif-
ferentiate velocity data into acceleration data and to integrate
velocity data into displacement data. This would require addi-
tional storage space. In this study, we use GPU to perform near
real-time computing of acceleration and displacement data so
that the data storage space can be reduced. This is because data
post-processing is no longer required to produce acceleration
and displacement data. The evaluation of earthquake simula-
tion data is a complex task that requires signiﬁcant training.
Thus, we propose to use volume rendering to better understand
and analyze time-varying earthquake ground-motion data,
including acceleration, velocity, and displacement. A case study
of the 1999 Chi-Chi earthquake in Taiwan is presented in
this paper. We used CUDA to implement volume rendering
(ray casting), numerical integration (trapezoidal quadrature),
and numerical differentiation (centered ﬁnite difference) and
achieved a speedup of approximately 100 times faster than on
a CPU.
Keywords-volume rendering; CUDA; earthquake;
I. INTRODUCTION
In recent years, data from scientiﬁc simulations and
scanning devices have grown rapidly in size. Dual-core,
low-end notebook computers, which are now being used
as many-core workstation computers, are inadequate for the
data processing requirements of researchers and scientists.
Thus, parallel computing will become increasingly impor-
tant. Software developers will need to support a variety
of parallel computing platforms and technologies to meet
the requirements of an increasingly sophisticated base of
users. Multithreaded graphical interfaces are expected be at
the forefront of parallel computing. Numerical integration
and differentiation techniques are needed for earthquake
transformation because the raw data is too large to process
on the CPU, where the transform can take up to 17 minutes
in this study. The data type of earthquake data is ﬂoat and
there are three channels to process, which results in large
computational time and resource consumption.
For the past decades, graphics processing units (GPUs)
have the advantage of high arithmetic throughput, which
can overcome CPU bottleneck problems. GPU computing
offers several advantages and will be increasingly important
in the future. CUDA (Compute United Device Architecture)
programming language was launched in 2006. CUDA is
a parallel programming model, where the software envi-
ronment is designed to maintain a low learning curve for
programmers familiar with standard programming languages
such as C. For this reason, CUDA is the ﬁrst language
speciﬁcally designed to facilitate general-purpose computing
on GPUs.
Figure 1. The 1999 Chi-Chi earthquake occurred on the Chelungpu fault,
the hanging wall moves up relative to the footwall. (a) The blue marks
indicate the locations of over 446 TSMIP stations that recorded the Chi-Chi
earthquake; the red cross indicates the location of epicenter. (b) Snapshots
of acceleration wave-ﬁeld map at UTC 17:47:50.
The objective of this study is to use GPU to implement
the volume rendering, the numerical integration (trapezoidal
quadrature), and numerical differentiation (centered ﬁnite
difference). Using numerical methods, the ground-motion
velocity data can be converted to acceleration or displace-
ment data. We combine the numerical method and volume
rendering to perform near real-time rendering of earthquake
ground-motion data to better understand earthquakes and
make it easier to observe details. Volume rendering is
a computer graphics technique for revealing the internal
structure of a volume data. It has proved to be effective for
the display and visual analysis of volumetric scalar ﬁelds in
2012 IEEE 14th International Conference on High Performance Computing and Communications
978-0-7695-4749-7/12 $26.00 © 2012 IEEE
DOI 10.1109/HPCC.2012.114
812
II. RUN-TIME CPU COMPUTING AND RENDERING
CUDA (Compute Uniﬁed Device Architecture) is a paral-
lel computing architecture. It gives developers access to the
virtual instruction set and memory of the parallel computa-
tional elements in the GPU. With CUDA, the GPUs have be-
come accessible for computation the way CPUs are. Unlike
CPUs however, GPUs have a parallel throughput architecture
that emphasizes executing many concurrent threads slowly,
rather than executing a single thread very quickly. In this
study, there are two different phases involved in rendering
implementation: (i) CPU-Based and (ii) GPU-Based phases.
The former makes best use of the sequential computing
capability of the CPU, while the latter uses the GPU for
large-scale scientiﬁc computing to optimize the computation
time. The GPU-Based phase can be divided into two models:
the graphics model and the CUDA model. Implementation
of the graphics model requires the use of specialized shading
languages such as Cg or GLSL, which is complicated and
has a steep learning curve. In this research, we focus on the
CUDA Model.
A. Direct Volume Rendering
Volume visualization has been popular since the early
1980s, when the medical community ﬁrst used this technique
to handle 3D data from CT and MRI scanners. Volume
rendering can be used to obtain an initial overall view
of the data, and by changing transfer functions, we can
incrementally focus on features that we want to observe.
As the visualization is made of semitransparent material
that can emit, transmit, and absorb light, it allows us to
observe the data within or even see through it. By changing
the material’s optical properties, we can achieve different
lighting effects. Volume rendering is a technique used to
display a 2D projection of a 3D discretely sampled data
set. Three steps are involved in this technique: Step 1. Treat
the volume data as a 3D array of scalar values, sampling
incrementally through the volume with the volume-rendering
algorithm. Step 2. Use transfer function to map the color
and opacity to a scalar within the volume, and compute
the contribution and the distance of different samples using
the volume-rendering integral. Step 3. After classifying a
sample, the last step before moving to the next sample is to
blend it with the previous samples using alpha value. In other
words, this step is to blend these classiﬁed steps together to
form an image.
Figure 4 shows the volume rendering of the acceleration
volume data. The temporal information of the ground-
motion data s visualized spatially so that the time history can
be directly observed. This approach brings new perspectives
in studying ground-motion data, providing seismologists
new visual analytical tools for verifying seismic mechanism.
Visualization reveals the sequence of seismic wave initiation,
propagation, attenuation over time, and energy releasing
events.
Figure 4. Volume rendering of Chi-Chi earthquake ground-motion accel-
eration volume data. The energetic area (with reddish color tones) can be
clearly identiﬁed, providing a good indication of the epicenter location.
Figure 5 shows a user interface of the transfer function.
A transfer function is a simple mapping from scalar values
to color and opacity. It is generally represented by a lookup
table, which can be accessed using scalar values and uses
linear interpolation to represent a continuous range with a
ﬁnite number of entries.
Figure 5. The user interface of transfer function design. For a given
input value, the visual panel shows its mapping to a certain output color
multiplied the corresponding transparency factor. The transparency curve
editing panel allows the user to use mouse to draw a curve which represents
the opacity value (between 0.0 and 1.0). The number of triangles in the
triangle control panel can be increased or decreased. The palette panel has
a HSV color wheel allows user to modify the hue, saturation, and value of
a color.
B. Numerical trapezoidal quadrature
The volume data we can get from earthquake measure-
ment stations is usually just the acceleration, which is not
enough for seismology or earthquake engineering scientists.
814
Algorithm 1 The pseudo code of the integration transfor-
mation program using CUDA
1: int tidX = blockDim.x*blockIdx.x+threadIdx.x;
2: int tidY = blockDim.y*blockIdx.y+threadIdx.y;
3: if ((tidX >= imageW) or (tidY >= imageH)) return;
4: for the time axis do
5: if (keep the index in the range of time axis)
6: apply the Trapezoidal Quadrature
7: Rule in every voxel along the axis
8: add all the result as a value in the voxel
9: end for
Algorithm 2 The pseudo code of the differentiation trans-
formation program using CUDA
1: int tidX = blockDim.x*blockIdx.x+threadIdx.x;
2: int tidY = blockDim.y*blockIdx.y+threadIdx.y;
3: if ((tidX >= imageW) or (tidY >= imageH)) return;
4: for within the time range do
5: Output vector = (previousvoxel−nextvoxel)/2× timestep
6: end for
III. RESULTS AND DISCUSSION
We evaluate our implementations on a PC with an Intel
Core i7 CPU, 3.0 GB of memory, and a GTX580 graphics
card with 1.5 GB of video memory, running Windows 7.
The graphics card has 16 SMs (Streaming Multiprocessors)
or 512 SP (Stream Processors) cores in total.
With the trapezoidal quadrature rule on CUDA, we can
convert the acceleration ﬁeld into the velocity and displace-
ment ﬁeld, but this is inadequate if we want to both observe
the results and compare them. The data size is too large
to process in the CPU and furthermore, it is inconvenient
to load the new data that is produced after the processing
and then render the result. Thus, we propose the idea
of combining the CUDA volume renderer, the trapezoidal
quadrature rule, and the centered ﬁnite difference method
to implement a tool that can transform them to different
ﬁelds in a small amount of time. The conversion time
information is shown as Table I and Table II (for trapezoidal
quadrature), and in Table III (for ﬁnite-difference). From
Table I, which presents the transformation information to
switch from acceleration ﬁeld to velocity ﬁeld, we can see
that if the CPU is used for computation, it will take nearly
17 minutes to complete this task. The GPU only requires 8
seconds, which could save a lot of time. The same applies to
Table II, which transforms the data from the velocity ﬁeld
to the displacement ﬁeld. In this case, the CUDA version
is 140 times faster than the CPU version. In Table III,
the transformation time information for differentiating the
ground velocity ﬁeld to ground acceleration ﬁeld is shown.
Due to less complex computation involved, we note that the
speedup is not as high as for trapezoidal quadrature.
Some features of the Chi-Chi earthquake from the ground
acceleration ﬁeld, ground velocity ﬁeld, and ground dis-
placement ﬁeld data, based on [5] and [6] are listed below:
(1) The peak ground acceleration (PGA) is generally higher

in the northern part of the source region. (2) The shaking
motion occurs along the northward rupture direction. Due to
the northward rupture propagation during the earthquake, the
ground motions are characterized by long periods and large
amplitudes in north Taiwan. In the central area, the ground
motion is relatively weak. (3) The slip in the southern part
of the fault shows a relatively low slip rate with a longer
duration. (4) Toward the northern section of the Chelungpu
fault, a decrease in ground acceleration was accompanied
by an increase in ground velocity and ground displacement.
(5) In the southern part, waveforms had lower amplitude
but higher frequency. Conversely, large amplitudes and long
periods dominate the waveforms in the northern stations
because of the strong directivity effect.
IV. CONCLUSIONS
CUDA makes use of the uniﬁed architecture design of
most current GPUs from NVIDIA. In this study, three
different methods were implemented: ray casting, trape-
zoidal quadrature rule, and the centered ﬁnite difference
method. The CPU version of the trapezoidal quadrature rule
was also implemented as a reference to compare against
CUDA implementations. The Chi-Chi earthquake data was
used as the source data for ray casting and the trapezoidal
quadrature rule. Implementations with CUDA were 141
times faster than the CPU based version when converting
ground acceleration ﬁeld into ground velocity ﬁeld, and
145 times faster when converting velocity ﬁeld into ground
displacement ﬁeld. With the tool we created, we can switch

Geophysical Research Abstracts
Vol. 14, EGU2012-4008, 2012
EGU General Assembly 2012
© Author(s) 2012
Earthquake-triggered Tsaoling landslide mechanics and dynamic process
revealed by discrete element method
K.-J. Chang (1), R.-F. Chen (2,3), Y.-C. Chan (3), C.-Y. Kuo (4), and C.-H. Weng (1)
(1) Department of Civil Engineering, National Taipei University of Technology, Taipei, Taiwan, R.O.C. (epidote@ntut.edu.tw,
+886-2-27814518), (2) Department of Geology, Chinese Culture University, Taipei, Taiwan, R.O.C., (3) Institute of Earth
Sciences, Academia Sinica, Taipei, Taiwan, R.O.C., (4) Research Center for Applied Sciences, Academia Sinica, Taipei,
R.O.C.
The high-speed large-scaled Tsaoling rock-and-soil avalanche is the largest landslides triggered by the Chi-Chi
earthquake (Taiwan, 1999). In order to characterize the landslide mechanics and sliding behavior, this study
integrates the geological and morphological features, strong motion seismostation record during block sliding on
the sliding surface, and numerical simulation. The morphological analysis was performed by interpreting aerial
photos taken before and at several times after the Chi-Chi earthquake. The topography of the landslide was studied
by studying several 2m resolution digital elevation models (DEMs) generated from the aerial photos taken at
different times. The comparison between the topographies before and after the slide allows precise calculation of
the initial volume of rock and soil mobilized in the landslide, as well as the geometry and thickness of the landslide
deposit. Field observations at different scales were also carried along the sliding surface and the landslide deposit
and gave new insights into the mechanical behavior of the landslide, and the subsequent geomorphologic evolution
of the landslide site.
The major sliding surface is situated between two massive sandstones by a metric friable fine layer composing
of fine layered shale, silty mudstone and interlayered beds, and is characterizing by a smooth, gentile and planar
surface. The major slid mass situated on the upper slope, is an isolated hill and been daylighted. The estimated
volume of the initial rocke avalanche is about 125.5 Mm3 and 138 Mm3 for the depleted and accumulation zones,
respectively, indicating an increase in volume due to fragmentation. The average thickness was about 150 - 170m,
up to 195 m thick of the slid mass. Whereas about 4/5 of the slid mass transport across the river and deposit around
the Taochiashan hill. The hill, composed of rock debris generated by the previous events, is about 140 m higher
than the Chinshui riverbed before the earthquake. The transported debris was about 30 - 90 m thick, covered on the
preexisting debris deposit hill and around the river channel. The debris formed a dammed lake, with a maximum
volume of 45 Mm3.
Based on DTMs data sets, field observations, the discrete element method - PFC3D is adapts to analyze the
triggering mechanism and sling dynamic process. The presence and the coupling effect from the strong ground
excitation and high pore water pressure is the essential factor to triggering the landslide event. The results shows
that the best fit between the deposit topography of the post-event DTM and numerical simulations, the fictional
coefficient of the sliding surface is as low as 0.087. The maximum sliding speed is as high as 87.2 m/s, the result
coincide with the seismic record from the nearby strong motion seismic record.
Geophysical Research Abstracts
Vol. 14, EGU2012-4438, 2012
EGU General Assembly 2012
© Author(s) 2012
Landslide events in Tsaoling and their effect on sediment flux
distributions,Taiwan
R.-F. Chen (1,2), K.-J. Chang (3), Y.-C. Chan (2), C.-W. Lin (4), and C.-Y. Kuo (5)
(1) Department of Geology, Chinese Culture University, 55 Hwa-Kang Road, Yang-Ming-Shan, Taipei 11114, Taiwan, (2)
Institute of Earth Sciences, Academia Sinica, P.O. Box 1-55 Nankang, Taipei 11529, Taiwan, (3) Department of Civil
Engineering, National Taipei University of Technology, Taipei 10608, Taiwan, (4) Department of Earth Sciences, National
Cheng Kung University, Tainan 70101, Taiwan , (5) Research Center for Applied Sciences, Academia Sinica, Taipei 11529,
Taiwan
In the climatic and geodynamic context of Taiwan, with large annual rainfall and strong deformation and uplift, the
erosion processes are very active. The evaluation of the erosion rates plays an important role for both the study of
the mountain building and related geological processes and the natural hazard mitigation purposes. Frequent earth-
quakes affect the stability of mountain slopes, and landslides favour river erosion of disrupted masses. As for many
rivers in Taiwan, large changes in water discharge occur with time, as a function of variable rainfall and typhoon
occurrence. This highly irregular flow regime has caused severe damage and human losses. To understand the po-
tential of landslide and position of potential landslide area is important for protection of the property and life and
people, which helps to improve the land use management in the hazardous area. On September 21 1999, a catas-
trophic earthquake occurred in the mountainous Tsaoling area in Central-Western Taiwan, at epicentral distance of
about 35 km. Chi-Chi earthquake (ML=7.3) triggered two huge landslides at Jiufengerhshan and Tsaoling, Killing
39 and 29 persons, respectively. We focus on the Tsaoling landslide, form the point of view of historical landslide
event, the occurrence of successive landslides in the Tsaoling area during the last century. Historical catastrophic
dip slope failures have repeatedly occurred, triggered by heavy rainfalls, as in 1942, 1951 and 1979, or by destruc-
tive earthquake. The catastrophic of Chi-Chi earthquake which mobilized about 0.125 km3 of rock and soil that
slide across Chingshui River and created a 5-km-long dam. To understand the impact of earthquake induced land-
slide on short-lived sediment budgets and suspended sediment transported in the Chingshui River. In this study, we
analyzed the rapid topographical changes during the 7 years following the event, with deep incision of the landslide
mass by the Chingshui River. Erosion rates have been estimated for the interval 1958-2009 from measurements
of river suspended-sediment discharge over 5 stations in the mountain regions. We quantify the sediment transfer
in the rivers running from high mountains to the sea, and hence the erosion rate, by combining large numbers of
water discharge data with smaller numbers of sediment content data. Our observations from the Chingshui River
near Tsaoling indicate that despite upstream sediment accumulation resulting from landslide damming, landslides
undoubtedly facilitate erosion, because disrupted landslide masses are quickly eroded. The study of the Tsaoling
landslide suggests that the probability for further major landslide events is high, which deserves consideration in
terms of natural hazard mitigation.

1) 台灣地區的專家學者可能由於地緣關係，較少參與此一大會，這也是本人首次
參加。反觀，印度、日本和中國大陸對於此一會議的參與相對較為踴躍。如上
文所述，此一會議雖在歐洲舉辦，但參與人士來自世界各地，有相當大的影響
力；為增加和歐洲以及其他地區遙測相關學術和產業的交流，爾後應多加以推
廣，並鼓勵台灣地區學者專家踴躍參與。
2) SPIE Remote Sensing大會的論文除需先經全文審稿外，尚要先註冊才能排進議
程。而且，會議論文集於會後集結才出版，若未至現場報告(no show)則不加以
收錄。如此較可保障論文及研討會品質。然而，此次大會仍有數篇印度和伊朗
籍作者之論文未出席報告，日後國內相關研討會舉辦對於來自這些國家和地區
的論文應多加注意。
3) 舉辦國際研討會是展現學術研發實力的一個適當場合，中央大學太空及遙測中
心和中華民國航測及遙感探測學會經多年努力後終於於去年成功爭取到主辦
2011年之第三十二屆亞洲遙測研討會。此舉相信對促進國際學術交流與合作、
促進研究與相關產業升級、提昇台灣國際能見度、推廣國際觀光等都將有極大
的助益。而 SPIE Remote Sensing也曾經舉辦過一次亞太地區的大會，日後也是
適合爭取於台灣舉辦的相關國際研討會。
5) 本次會議參展的廠商非常多元，除了歐洲地區的廠商外，尚有許多美加等地的
跨國大廠參展。所展出的產品、技術、和服務也非常先進，也有很多跨領域的
產品和應用，吸引與會各國人士極大的興趣。反觀國內相關產業的廠商，不但
規模小，且多專注國內的市場；未來應該多充實設備和技術，擴展國際市場，
找尋相關產業的藍海。

2. REMOTE SENSING AND SPATIAL ANALYSIS FOR LANDSLIDES
With the ability to cover a large area in a short time and to detect land-cover changes, remote sensing has been successfully
utilized to investigate and monitor landslides. For example, Nichole and Wong produced detailed landslide inventories
using multiple satellite remote sensing images.2 Remote sensing also contributed to the assessment of landslide hazards in
mountainous environments.3 Similar approach was also employed to investigate landslides and vegetation cover changes
after earthquake.4
In addition to image-based change detection and monitoring, remote sensing are often coupled with spatial analysis
functions of Geographic Information Systems (GIS) to perform in-depth, quantitative analysis of landslides and other natu-
ral hazards. For example, previous studies5,6 utilized regression analysis in GIS systems to generate landslide susceptibility
maps. Similar spatial analysis was also applied to the prediction of landslide hazards.7 Another useful application of inte-
grating remote sensing and spatial analysis is to identify spatial relationship between landslides and their causative factors8
in order to better understand the risk of landslide hazards.
These examples indicate that remote sensing and spatial analysis are effective means for landslide detection, moni-
toring, and analysis. However, landslides in different regions have various characteristics. Different data sources also
require different algorithms and methodology to process and analyze. The rest of this paper will describe an integrated and
systematic framework to utilize satellite imagery and spatial analysis for detecting and monitoring landslides in Taiwan.
3. METHODOLOGY
The developed integrated landslide detection and monitoring system is based on the change detection of multi-temporal
satellite images. The framework is separated into three phases, including pre-processing, landslide detection, and spatial
analysis. The primary data required for landslide detection and monitoring are SPOT and FORMOSAT-2 satellite images.
SPOT and FORMOSAT-2 sensors can acquire data in multiple spectral bands and the spatial resolutions of the images are
between 2 to 5 meters in panchromatic and 8 to 20 meters in multi-spectral. In particular, FORMOSAT-2 has an unique
daily-revisit capability, making it an idea data sources for hazard investigation and monitoring, especially for emergency
circumstances. In addition to satellite images, digital elevation models (DEMs), topographic maps, land-cover/land-use
maps and other spatial datasets are also used as supporting data for the analysis.

where SB is the spectral bandwidth and SI is the solar irradiance at the top of atmosphere (TOA); and θ is the solar zenith
angle.
For the analysis of multi-temporal satellite images, after converted to apparent reﬂectance, the image data should be
normalized to further reduce biases.13,14 The normalization is based on pseudo invariant features (PIF) selected from
the images. The selection of PIF pixels can be done interactively. Good PIF candidates include deep clean water, dense
forest, man-made objects (roads, bridges, parking lots, buildings etc.), bare grounds and the like. Another option is to
automatically select PIFs according to statistical characters of the images. For example, Fig. 4 shows the scatter plot of the
same infrared band from two SPOT images covering the same area. The highly-correlated pixels indicated in the ﬁgure are
considered PIFs of the two images.
Figure 4: Pseudo invariant feature selection from scatter plot of two images.
3.2 Landslide Detection
Most landslides occur in hills or mountainous regions, so they are likely to exhibit signiﬁcant vegetation coverage changes
in satellite images. Therefore, Normalized Difference Vegetation Index (NDVI) is an effective measure to identify possible
landslides from multi-temporal images. Based on previous experiences,15 the developed landslide detection and analysis
framework uses a NDVI ﬁltering rule (Eq. ) to identify preliminary landslide candidates.
NDV Ipre −NDV Ipost ≥ 0.3 ∧ NDV Ipost ≤ 0.1 (2)
where NDV Ipre and NDV Ipost are NDVI values of the pre- and post-event images, respectively. The thresholds are
determined empirically and can be changed based on NDVI values of the images to analyze.
NDVI ﬁltering is considered a fast but preliminary method for landslide detection. The results are integrated with
change vector analysis16,17 (CVA) of the images. CVA identiﬁes changed and unchanged pixels from multi-temporal
images according to change vectors in different spectral bands. The magnitude of a change vector (D, Eq. 3) reﬂects the
change in intensity, while the angle, θ, between the two spectral vectors (t, r) forming the change vector is correlated to
the change in color (Eq. 4). The integration between NDVI ﬁltering and CVA results is performed using spatial Boolean
operations, i.e., spatial union for identiﬁed landslides and spatial subtraction of non-landslides from the union result.

The second example is the long-term monitoring of the Shimen Reservoir watershed in northern Taiwan. Landslides
are also commonly induced by heavy rainfall in the watershed and the debris ﬂushed into the reservoir has become a
serious threat to the operation of the reservoir and water supply. Using similar techniques mentioned above, the developed
system can detect and analyze landslides effectively. For example, Fig. 8 displays a typical riverbank landslide and
an isolated small-scale landslide detected in the watershed. A ﬁeld investigation form is automatically generated after
detecting a possible landslide. The form consists of subsets of satellite images, topographic map, trafﬁc route suggestion
map, and itemized ﬁelds to be ﬁlled out by investigators. The watershed management authority will pass on the form
to dispatched patrols to conduct ﬁeld investigations and the results are fed back to the project to improve the landslide
detection algorithms.
Figure 8: Examples of landslide detection in Shimen Reservoir watershed.

總計畫：這是三年期整合型研究案的第二年，除了持續第一年的三維雷射掃描儀現地掃描
工作之外，也進行猴山岳邊坡地形剖面分析、3D 及超高解析度影像問卷研究、雨量預警程
式開發、猴山岳邊坡沖蝕量估算、USLE 公式驗證、眾人分工樹木移動量研究（Turk）及影
像質點樹木移動量分析（PIV），總計指導完成三篇相關的碩士論文，並投稿 10 篇的國際
研討會論文，擔任了一個國際研討會的 Program Committee Member (ICSI 2012)及另一個
國際研討會的 Scientific Committee Member (Soil Bio- and Eco-Engineering 2012)，
所購買的儀器和所收集的資料也在每兩個月一次的工作會議中與各子計畫分享，並協助各
子計畫進行相關的現地工作，研究成果豐碩且具有應用價值，預期本研究案的光達掃描技
術及相關創新邊坡分析方法仍將有進一步發展的可能性及多方面應用的潛力。 
 
子計畫一：本子計畫延續第一年收集與討論多時段多來源地形資料精度的議題，本年度著
重於分析各類地形資料間的不確定性分析，以分析不同時期、不同精度、不同解析度的地
形資料整合使用時的議題，並提供給其他子計畫團隊使用。而配合本計畫採購之地面光達
掃瞄儀，為記錄猴山岳研究區域的地形變化，需以絕對座標記錄點雲資料，擬定研究區域
的控制點與導線網測量計畫與維護計畫。 
 
子計畫二：[學術成就]：進行點雲數據視覺分析個案研究，發表 SCI 期刊論文三篇。[技
術創新]：建置點雲數據處理顯示平臺，進行掃描數據的資訊查詢、資訊擷取、資訊分析
